### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpec

AWSManagedControlPlaneSpec defines the desired state of an Amazon EKS Cluster.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalTags**|{str:str}|AdditionalTags is an optional set of tags to add to AWS resources managed by the AWS provider, in addition to the<br />ones added by default.||
|**addons**|[[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecAddonsItems0](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecaddonsitems0)]|Addons defines the EKS addons to enable with the EKS cluster.||
|**associateOIDCProvider**|bool|AssociateOIDCProvider can be enabled to automatically create an identity<br />provider for the controller for use with IAM roles for service accounts|False|
|**bastion**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecBastion](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecbastion)|bastion||
|**controlPlaneEndpoint**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecControlPlaneEndpoint](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespeccontrolplaneendpoint)|control plane endpoint||
|**disableVPCCNI**|bool|DisableVPCCNI indicates that the Amazon VPC CNI should be disabled. With EKS clusters the<br />Amazon VPC CNI is automatically installed into the cluster. For clusters where you want<br />to use an alternate CNI this option provides a way to specify that the Amazon VPC CNI<br />should be deleted. You cannot set this to true if you are using the<br />Amazon VPC CNI addon.|False|
|**eksClusterName**|str|EKSClusterName allows you to specify the name of the EKS cluster in<br />AWS. If you don't specify a name then a default name will be created<br />based on the namespace and name of the managed control plane.||
|**encryptionConfig**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecEncryptionConfig](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecencryptionconfig)|encryption config||
|**endpointAccess**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecEndpointAccess](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecendpointaccess)|endpoint access||
|**iamAuthenticatorConfig**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecIamAuthenticatorConfig](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespeciamauthenticatorconfig)|iam authenticator config||
|**identityRef**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecIdentityRef](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecidentityref)|identity ref||
|**imageLookupBaseOS**|str|ImageLookupBaseOS is the name of the base operating system used to look<br />up machine images when a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this<br />will be used for all cluster machines unless a machine specifies a<br />different ImageLookupBaseOS.||
|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up machine images when<br />a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.<br />Supports substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base<br />OS and kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to look up machine images when a<br />machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.||
|**kubeProxy**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecKubeProxy](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespeckubeproxy)|kube proxy||
|**logging**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecLogging](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespeclogging)|logging||
|**network**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecNetwork](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecnetwork)|network||
|**oidcIdentityProviderConfig**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecOidcIdentityProviderConfig](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecoidcidentityproviderconfig)|oidc identity provider config||
|**region**|str|The AWS Region the cluster lives in.||
|**roleAdditionalPolicies**|[str]|RoleAdditionalPolicies allows you to attach additional polices to<br />the control plane role. You must enable the EKSAllowAddRoles<br />feature flag to incorporate these into the created role.||
|**roleName**|str|RoleName specifies the name of IAM role that gives EKS<br />permission to make API calls. If the role is pre-existing<br />we will treat it as unmanaged and not delete it on<br />deletion. If the EKSEnableIAM feature flag is true<br />and no name is supplied then a role is created.||
|**secondaryCidrBlock**|str|SecondaryCidrBlock is the additional CIDR range to use for pod IPs.<br />Must be within the 100.64.0.0/10 or 198.19.0.0/16 range.||
|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the bastion host. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||
|**tokenMethod**|"iam-authenticator" | "aws-cli"|TokenMethod is used to specify the method for obtaining a client token for communicating with EKS<br />iam-authenticator - obtains a client token using iam-authentictor<br />aws-cli - obtains a client token using the AWS CLI<br />Defaults to iam-authenticator|"iam-authenticator"|
|**version**|str|Version defines the desired Kubernetes version. If no version number<br />is supplied then the latest version of Kubernetes that EKS supports<br />will be used.||
|**vpcCni**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecVpcCni](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedcontrolplanespecvpccni)|vpc cni||

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecBastion

Bastion contains options to configure the bastion host.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**allowedCIDRBlocks**|[str]|AllowedCIDRBlocks is a list of CIDR blocks allowed to access the bastion host.<br />They are set as ingress rules for the Bastion host's Security Group (defaults to 0.0.0.0/0).||
|**ami**|str|AMI will use the specified AMI to boot the bastion. If not specified,<br />the AMI will default to one picked out in public space.||
|**disableIngressRules**|bool|DisableIngressRules will ensure there are no Ingress rules in the bastion host's security group.<br />Requires AllowedCIDRBlocks to be empty.||
|**enabled**|bool|Enabled allows this provider to create a bastion host instance<br />with a public ip to access the VPC private network.||
|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType will use the specified instance type for the bastion. If not specified,<br />Cluster API Provider AWS will use t3.micro for all regions except us-east-1, where t2.micro<br />will be the default.||

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecNetworkSubnetsItems0

SubnetSpec configures an AWS Subnet.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZone**|str|AvailabilityZone defines the availability zone to use for this subnet in the cluster's region.||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.||
|**id** `required`|str|ID defines a unique identifier to reference this resource.<br />If you're bringing your subnet, set the AWS subnet-id here, it must start with `subnet-`.<br /><br />When the VPC is managed by CAPA, and you'd like the provider to create a subnet for you,<br />the id can be set to any placeholder value that does not start with `subnet-`;<br />upon creation, the subnet AWS identifier will be populated in the `ResourceID` field and<br />the `id` field is going to be used as the subnet name. If you specify a tag<br />called `Name`, it takes precedence.||
|**ipv6CidrBlock**|str|IPv6CidrBlock is the IPv6 CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />A subnet can have an IPv4 and an IPv6 address.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isIpv6**|bool|IsIPv6 defines the subnet as an IPv6 subnet. A subnet is IPv6 when it is associated with a VPC that has IPv6 enabled.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isPublic**|bool|IsPublic defines the subnet as a public subnet. A subnet is public when it is associated with a route table that has a route to an internet gateway.||
|**natGatewayId**|str|NatGatewayID is the NAT gateway id associated with the subnet.<br />Ignored unless the subnet is managed by the provider, in which case this is set on the public subnet where the NAT gateway resides. It is then used to determine routes for private subnets in the same AZ as the public subnet.||
|**parentZoneName**|str|ParentZoneName is the zone name where the current subnet's zone is tied when<br />the zone is a Local Zone.<br /><br />The subnets in Local Zone or Wavelength Zone locations consume the ParentZoneName<br />to select the correct private route table to egress traffic to the internet.||
|**resourceID**|str|ResourceID is the subnet identifier from AWS, READ ONLY.<br />This field is populated when the provider manages the subnet.||
|**routeTableId**|str|RouteTableID is the routing table id associated with the subnet.||
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
|**zoneType**|"availability-zone" | "local-zone" | "wavelength-zone"|ZoneType defines the type of the zone where the subnet is created.<br /><br />The valid values are availability-zone, local-zone, and wavelength-zone.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type availability-zone (regular) is always selected to create cluster<br />resources, like Load Balancers, NAT Gateways, Contol Plane nodes, etc.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type local-zone or wavelength-zone is not eligible to automatically create<br />regular cluster resources.<br /><br />The public subnet in availability-zone or local-zone is associated with regular public<br />route table with default route entry to a Internet Gateway.<br /><br />The public subnet in wavelength-zone is associated with a carrier public<br />route table with default route entry to a Carrier Gateway.<br /><br />The private subnet in the availability-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry to a NAT Gateway created in that zone.<br /><br />The private subnet in the local-zone or wavelength-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry re-using the NAT Gateway in the Region (preferred from the<br />parent zone, the zone type availability-zone in the region, or first table available).||

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecOidcIdentityProviderConfig

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**clientId**|str|This is also known as audience. The ID for the client application that makes<br />authentication requests to the OpenID identity provider.||
|**groupsClaim**|str|The JWT claim that the provider uses to return your groups.||
|**groupsPrefix**|str|The prefix that is prepended to group claims to prevent clashes with existing<br />names (such as system: groups). For example, the valueoidc: will create group<br />names like oidc:engineering and oidc:infra.||
|**identityProviderConfigName**|str|The name of the OIDC provider configuration.<br /><br />IdentityProviderConfigName is a required field||
|**issuerUrl**|str|The URL of the OpenID identity provider that allows the API server to discover<br />public signing keys for verifying tokens. The URL must begin with https://<br />and should correspond to the iss claim in the provider's OIDC ID tokens.<br />Per the OIDC standard, path components are allowed but query parameters are<br />not. Typically the URL consists of only a hostname, like https://server.example.org<br />or https://example.com. This URL should point to the level below .well-known/openid-configuration<br />and must be publicly accessible over the internet.||
|**requiredClaims**|{str:str}|The key value pairs that describe required claims in the identity token.<br />If set, each claim is verified to be present in the token with a matching<br />value. |**tags**|{str:str}|tags to apply to oidc identity provider association||
|**usernameClaim**|str|The JSON Web Token (JWT) claim to use as the username. The default is sub,<br />which is expected to be a unique identifier of the end user. You can choose<br />other claims, such as email or name, depending on the OpenID identity provider.<br />Claims other than email are prefixed with the issuer URL to prevent naming<br />clashes with other plug-ins.||
|**usernamePrefix**|str|The prefix that is prepended to username claims to prevent clashes with existing<br />names. If you do not provide this field, and username is a value other than<br />email, the prefix defaults to issuerurl#. You can use the value - to disable<br />all prefixing.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpec

Spec for this AWSClusterControllerIdentity.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**allowedNamespaces**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpecAllowedNamespaces](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsclustercontrolleridentityspecallowednamespaces)|allowed namespaces||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpecAllowedNamespaces

AllowedNamespaces is used to identify which namespaces are allowed to use the identity from. Namespaces can be selected either using an array of namespaces or with label selector. An empty allowedNamespaces object indicates that AWSClusters can use this identity from any namespace. If this object is nil, no namespaces will be allowed (default behaviour, if this field is not provided) A namespace should be either in the NamespaceList or match with Selector to use the identity.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**list**|[str]|An nil or empty list indicates that AWSClusters cannot use the identity from any namespace.||
|**selector**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpecAllowedNamespacesSelector](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsclustercontrolleridentityspecallowednamespacesselector)|selector||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpecAllowedNamespacesSelector

An empty selector indicates that AWSClusters cannot use this AWSClusterIdentity from any namespace.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchExpressions**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpecAllowedNamespacesSelectorMatchExpressionsItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsclustercontrolleridentityspecallowednamespacesselectormatchexpressionsitems0)]|matchExpressions is a list of label selector requirements. The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels<br />map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the<br />operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterControllerIdentitySpecAllowedNamespacesSelectorMatchExpressionsItems0

A label selector requirement is a selector that contains values, a key, and an operator that relates the key and values.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|str|operator represents a key's relationship to a set of values.<br />Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn,<br />the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist,<br />the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic<br />merge patch.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterRoleIdentitySpec

Spec for this AWSClusterRoleIdentity.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**allowedNamespaces**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterRoleIdentitySpecAllowedNamespaces](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsclusterroleidentityspecallowednamespaces)|allowed namespaces||
|**durationSeconds**|int|The duration, in seconds, of the role session before it is renewed.||
|**externalID**|str|A unique identifier that might be required when you assume a role in another account.<br />If the administrator of the account to which the role belongs provided you with an<br />external ID, then provide that value in the ExternalId parameter. This value can be<br />any string, such as a passphrase or account number. A cross-account role is usually<br />set up to trust everyone in an account. Therefore, the administrator of the trusting<br />account might send an external ID to the administrator of the trusted account. That<br />way, only someone with the ID can assume the role, rather than everyone in the<br />account. For more information about the external ID, see How to Use an External ID<br />When Granting Access to Your AWS Resources to a Third Party in the IAM User Guide.||
|**inlinePolicy**|str|An IAM policy as a JSON-encoded string that you want to use as an inline session policy.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterRoleIdentitySpecAllowedNamespaces

AllowedNamespaces is used to identify which namespaces are allowed to use the identity from. Namespaces can be selected either using an array of namespaces or with label selector. An empty allowedNamespaces object indicates that AWSClusters can use this identity from any namespace. If this object is nil, no namespaces will be allowed (default behaviour, if this field is not provided) A namespace should be either in the NamespaceList or match with Selector to use the identity.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**list**|[str]|An nil or empty list indicates that AWSClusters cannot use the identity from any namespace.||
|**selector**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterRoleIdentitySpecAllowedNamespacesSelector](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsclusterroleidentityspecallowednamespacesselector)|selector||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterRoleIdentitySpecAllowedNamespacesSelector

An empty selector indicates that AWSClusters cannot use this AWSClusterIdentity from any namespace.

The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels<br />map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the<br />operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||

|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up machine images when<br />a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.<br />Supports substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base<br />OS and kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to look up machine images when a<br />machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.||
|**network**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSClusterSpecNetwork](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsclusterspecnetwork)|network||

|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the bastion host. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||

|**lastTransitionTime** `required`|str|Last time the condition transitioned from one status to another.<br />This should be when the underlying condition changed. If that is not known, then using the time when<br />the API field changed is acceptable.||
|**message**|str|A human readable message indicating details about the transition.<br />This field may be empty.||
|**reason**|str|The reason for the condition's last transition in CamelCase.<br />The specific API may choose whether or not this field is considered a guaranteed API.<br />This field may not be empty.||
|**severity**|str|Severity provides an explicit classification of Reason code, so the users or machines can immediately<br />understand the current situation and act accordingly.<br />The Severity field MUST be set only when Status=False.||
|**status** `required`|str|Status of the condition, one of True, False, Unknown.||
|**type** `required`|str|||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSFargateProfileStatus

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |

|**failureMessage**|str|FailureMessage will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the FargateProfile and will contain a more verbose string suitable<br />for logging and human consumption.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the FargateProfile's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of<br />FargateProfiles can be added as events to the FargateProfile<br />object and/or logged in the controller's output.||
|**failureReason**|str|FailureReason will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the FargateProfile and will contain a succinct value suitable<br />for machine interpretation.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the FargateProfile's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of<br />FargateProfiles can be added as events to the FargateProfile object<br />and/or logged in the controller's output.||
|**ready** `required`|bool|Ready denotes that the FargateProfile is available.|False|

|**defaultCoolDown**|str|The amount of time, in seconds, after a scaling activity completes before another scaling activity can start.<br />If no value is supplied by user a default value of 300 seconds is set||
|**maxSize** `required`|int|MaxSize defines the maximum size of the group.|1|
|**minSize** `required`|int|MinSize defines the minimum size of the group.|1|
|**mixedInstancesPolicy**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecMixedInstancesPolicy](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecmixedinstancespolicy)|mixed instances policy||
|**providerID**|str|ProviderID is the ARN of the associated ASG||
|**providerIDList**|[str]|ProviderIDList are the identification IDs of machine instances provided by the provider.<br />This field must match the provider IDs as seen on the node objects corresponding to a machine pool's machine instances.||
|**refreshPreferences**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecRefreshPreferences](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecrefreshpreferences)|refresh preferences||
|**subnets**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecSubnetsItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecsubnetsitems0)]|Subnets is an array of subnet configurations||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplate

AWSLaunchTemplate specifies the launch template and version to use when an instance is launched.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalSecurityGroups**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateAdditionalSecurityGroupsItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplateadditionalsecuritygroupsitems0)]|AdditionalSecurityGroups is an array of references to security groups that should be applied to the<br />instances. These security groups would be set in addition to any security groups defined<br />at the cluster level or in the actuator.||
|**ami**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateAmi](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplateami)|ami||
|**iamInstanceProfile**|str|The name or the Amazon Resource Name (ARN) of the instance profile associated<br />with the IAM role for the instance. The instance profile contains the IAM<br />role.||
|**imageLookupBaseOS**|str|ImageLookupBaseOS is the name of the base operating system to use for<br />image lookup the AMI is not set.||
|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up the image for this<br />machine It will be ignored if an explicit AMI is set. Supports<br />substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base OS and<br />kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to use for image lookup if AMI is not set.||
|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType is the type of instance to create. Example: m4.xlarge||
|**name**|str|The name of the launch template.||
|**rootVolume**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateRootVolume](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplaterootvolume)|root volume||
|**spotMarketOptions**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateSpotMarketOptions](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplatespotmarketoptions)|spot market options||
|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the instance. Valid values are empty string<br />(do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||
|**versionNumber**|int|VersionNumber is the version of the launch template that is applied.<br />Typically a new version is created when at least one of the following happens:<br />1) A new launch template spec is applied.<br />2) One or more parameters in an existing template is changed.<br />3) A new AMI is discovered.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolStatus

AWSMachinePoolStatus defines the observed state of AWSMachinePool.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**asgStatus**|str|ASGStatus is a status string returned by the autoscaling API.||
|**conditions**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolStatusConditionsItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolstatusconditionsitems0)]|Conditions defines current service state of the AWSMachinePool.||
|**failureMessage**|str|FailureMessage will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the Machine and will contain a more verbose string suitable<br />for logging and human consumption.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of Machines<br />can be added as events to the Machine object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**failureReason**|str|FailureReason will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the Machine and will contain a succinct value suitable<br />for machine interpretation.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of Machines<br />can be added as events to the Machine object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**instances**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSMachinePoolStatusInstancesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmachinepoolstatusinstancesitems0)]|Instances contains the status for each instance in the pool||
|**launchTemplateID**|str|The ID of the launch template||
|**launchTemplateVersion**|str|The version of the launch template||
|**ready**|bool|Ready is true when the provider resource is ready.||
|**replicas**|int|Replicas is the most recently observed number of replicas||

|**failureMessage**|str|FailureMessage will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the Machine and will contain a more verbose string suitable<br />for logging and human consumption.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of Machines<br />can be added as events to the Machine object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**failureReason**|str|FailureReason will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the Machine and will contain a succinct value suitable<br />for machine interpretation.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of Machines<br />can be added as events to the Machine object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**instanceState**|str|InstanceState is the state of the AWS instance for this machine.||
|**interruptible**|bool|Interruptible reports that this machine is using spot instances and can therefore be interrupted by CAPI when it receives a notice that the spot instance is to be terminated by AWS.<br />This will be set to true when SpotMarketOptions is not nil (i.e. this machine is using a spot instance).||
|**ready**|bool|Ready is true when the provider resource is ready.||

|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up the image for this<br />machine It will be ignored if an explicit AMI is set. Supports<br />substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base OS and<br />kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to use for image lookup if AMI is not set.||
|**instanceID**|str|InstanceID is the EC2 instance ID for this machine.||

|**networkInterfaces**|[str]|NetworkInterfaces is a list of ENIs to associate with the instance.<br />A maximum of 2 may be specified.||

|**providerID**|str|ProviderID is the unique identifier as specified by the cloud provider.||
|**publicIP**|bool|PublicIP specifies whether the instance should get a public IP.<br />Precedence for this setting is as follows:<br />1. This field if set<br />2. Cluster/flavor setting<br />3. Subnet default||

|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the instance. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**effect** `required`|"no-schedule" | "no-execute" | "prefer-no-schedule"|Effect specifies the effect for the taint||
|**key** `required`|str|Key is the key of the taint||
|**value** `required`|str|Value is the value of the taint||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedMachinePoolSpecUpdateConfig

UpdateConfig holds the optional config to control the behaviour of the update to the nodegroup.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**maxUnavailable**|int|MaxUnavailable is the maximum number of nodes unavailable at once during a version update.<br />Nodes will be updated in parallel. The maximum number is 100.||
|**maxUnavailablePrecentage**|int|MaxUnavailablePercentage is the maximum percentage of nodes unavailable during a version update. This<br />percentage of nodes will be updated in parallel, up to 100 nodes at once.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedMachinePoolStatus

AWSManagedMachinePoolStatus defines the observed state of AWSManagedMachinePool.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**conditions**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedMachinePoolStatusConditionsItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta1awsmanagedmachinepoolstatusconditionsitems0)]|Conditions defines current service state of the managed machine pool||
|**failureMessage**|str|FailureMessage will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the MachinePool and will contain a more verbose string suitable<br />for logging and human consumption.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the MachinePool's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of MachinePools<br />can be added as events to the MachinePool object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**failureReason**|str|FailureReason will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the MachinePool and will contain a succinct value suitable<br />for machine interpretation.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of MachinePools<br />can be added as events to the MachinePool object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**launchTemplateID**|str|The ID of the launch template||
|**launchTemplateVersion**|str|The version of the launch template||
|**ready** `required`|bool|Ready denotes that the AWSManagedMachinePool nodegroup has joined<br />the cluster|False|
|**replicas**|int|Replicas is the most recently observed number of replicas.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta1AWSManagedMachinePoolStatusConditionsItems0

Condition defines an observation of a Cluster API resource operational state.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**lastTransitionTime** `required`|str|Last time the condition transitioned from one status to another.<br />This should be when the underlying condition changed. If that is not known, then using the time when<br />the API field changed is acceptable.||
|**message**|str|A human readable message indicating details about the transition.<br />This field may be empty.||
|**reason**|str|The reason for the condition's last transition in CamelCase.<br />The specific API may choose whether or not this field is considered a guaranteed API.<br />This field may not be empty.||
|**severity**|str|Severity provides an explicit classification of Reason code, so the users or machines can immediately<br />understand the current situation and act accordingly.<br />The Severity field MUST be set only when Status=False.||
|**status** `required`|str|Status of the condition, one of True, False, Unknown.||
|**type** `required`|str|||

### BootstrapClusterxK8sIoV1beta2EKSConfigSpecDiskSetupFilesystemsItems0

Filesystem defines the file systems to be created.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**device** `required`|str|Device specifies the device name||
|**extraOpts**|[str]|ExtraOpts defined extra options to add to the command for creating the file system.||
|**filesystem** `required`|str|Filesystem specifies the file system type.||
|**label** `required`|str|Label specifies the file system label to be used. If set to None, no label is used.||
|**overwrite**|bool|Overwrite defines whether or not to overwrite any existing filesystem.<br />If true, any pre-existing file system will be destroyed. Use with Caution.||
|**partition**|str|Partition specifies the partition to use. The valid options are: "auto\|any", "auto", "any", "none", and <NUM>, where NUM is the actual partition number.||
### BootstrapClusterxK8sIoV1beta2EKSConfigSpecDiskSetupPartitionsItems0

Partition defines how to create and layout a partition.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**device** `required`|str|Device is the name of the device.||
|**layout** `required`|bool|Layout specifies the device layout.<br />If it is true, a single partition will be created for the entire device.<br />When layout is false, it means don't partition or ignore existing partitioning.||
|**overwrite**|bool|Overwrite describes whether to skip checks and create the partition if a partition or filesystem is found on the device.<br />Use with caution. Default is 'false'.||
|**tableType**|str|TableType specifies the tupe of partition table. The following are supported:<br />'mbr': default and setups a MS-DOS partition table<br />'gpt': setups a GPT partition table||

|**mounts**|[[str]]|Mounts specifies a list of mount points to be setup.||
|**ntp**|[BootstrapClusterxK8sIoV1beta2EKSConfigTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNtp](#bootstrapclusterxk8siov1beta2eksconfigtemplatespectemplatespecntp)|ntp||
|**pauseContainer**|[BootstrapClusterxK8sIoV1beta2EKSConfigTemplateSpecTemplateSpecPauseContainer](#bootstrapclusterxk8siov1beta2eksconfigtemplatespectemplatespecpausecontainer)|pause container||
|**postBootstrapCommands**|[str]|PostBootstrapCommands specifies extra commands to run after bootstrapping nodes to the cluster||
|**preBootstrapCommands**|[str]|PreBootstrapCommands specifies extra commands to run before bootstrapping nodes to the cluster||

|**imageLookupBaseOS**|str|ImageLookupBaseOS is the name of the base operating system used to look<br />up machine images when a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this<br />will be used for all cluster machines unless a machine specifies a<br />different ImageLookupBaseOS.||
|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up machine images when<br />a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.<br />Supports substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base<br />OS and kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to look up machine images when a<br />machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.||
|**kubeProxy**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecKubeProxy](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta2awsmanagedcontrolplanespeckubeproxy)|kube proxy||

|**partition**|str|Partition is the AWS security partition being used. Defaults to "aws"||
|**region**|str|The AWS Region the cluster lives in.||
|**roleAdditionalPolicies**|[str]|RoleAdditionalPolicies allows you to attach additional polices to<br />the control plane role. You must enable the EKSAllowAddRoles<br />feature flag to incorporate these into the created role.||
|**roleName**|str|RoleName specifies the name of IAM role that gives EKS<br />permission to make API calls. If the role is pre-existing<br />we will treat it as unmanaged and not delete it on<br />deletion. If the EKSEnableIAM feature flag is true<br />and no name is supplied then a role is created.||
|**secondaryCidrBlock**|str|SecondaryCidrBlock is the additional CIDR range to use for pod IPs.<br />Must be within the 100.64.0.0/10 or 198.19.0.0/16 range.||
|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the bastion host. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||
|**tokenMethod**|"iam-authenticator" | "aws-cli"|TokenMethod is used to specify the method for obtaining a client token for communicating with EKS<br />iam-authenticator - obtains a client token using iam-authentictor<br />aws-cli - obtains a client token using the AWS CLI<br />Defaults to iam-authenticator|"iam-authenticator"|
|**version**|str|Version defines the desired Kubernetes version. If no version number<br />is supplied then the latest version of Kubernetes that EKS supports<br />will be used.||

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecNetworkSubnetsItems0

SubnetSpec configures an AWS Subnet.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZone**|str|AvailabilityZone defines the availability zone to use for this subnet in the cluster's region.||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.||
|**id** `required`|str|ID defines a unique identifier to reference this resource.<br />If you're bringing your subnet, set the AWS subnet-id here, it must start with `subnet-`.<br /><br />When the VPC is managed by CAPA, and you'd like the provider to create a subnet for you,<br />the id can be set to any placeholder value that does not start with `subnet-`;<br />upon creation, the subnet AWS identifier will be populated in the `ResourceID` field and<br />the `id` field is going to be used as the subnet name. If you specify a tag<br />called `Name`, it takes precedence.||
|**ipv6CidrBlock**|str|IPv6CidrBlock is the IPv6 CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />A subnet can have an IPv4 and an IPv6 address.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isIpv6**|bool|IsIPv6 defines the subnet as an IPv6 subnet. A subnet is IPv6 when it is associated with a VPC that has IPv6 enabled.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isPublic**|bool|IsPublic defines the subnet as a public subnet. A subnet is public when it is associated with a route table that has a route to an internet gateway.||
|**natGatewayId**|str|NatGatewayID is the NAT gateway id associated with the subnet.<br />Ignored unless the subnet is managed by the provider, in which case this is set on the public subnet where the NAT gateway resides. It is then used to determine routes for private subnets in the same AZ as the public subnet.||
|**parentZoneName**|str|ParentZoneName is the zone name where the current subnet's zone is tied when<br />the zone is a Local Zone.<br /><br />The subnets in Local Zone or Wavelength Zone locations consume the ParentZoneName<br />to select the correct private route table to egress traffic to the internet.||
|**resourceID**|str|ResourceID is the subnet identifier from AWS, READ ONLY.<br />This field is populated when the provider manages the subnet.||
|**routeTableId**|str|RouteTableID is the routing table id associated with the subnet.||
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
|**zoneType**|"availability-zone" | "local-zone" | "wavelength-zone"|ZoneType defines the type of the zone where the subnet is created.<br /><br />The valid values are availability-zone, local-zone, and wavelength-zone.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type availability-zone (regular) is always selected to create cluster<br />resources, like Load Balancers, NAT Gateways, Contol Plane nodes, etc.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type local-zone or wavelength-zone is not eligible to automatically create<br />regular cluster resources.<br /><br />The public subnet in availability-zone or local-zone is associated with regular public<br />route table with default route entry to a Internet Gateway.<br /><br />The public subnet in wavelength-zone is associated with a carrier public<br />route table with default route entry to a Carrier Gateway.<br /><br />The private subnet in the availability-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry to a NAT Gateway created in that zone.<br /><br />The private subnet in the local-zone or wavelength-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry re-using the NAT Gateway in the Region (preferred from the<br />parent zone, the zone type availability-zone in the region, or first table available).||
### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecNetworkVpc

VPC configuration.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZoneSelection**|"Ordered" | "Random"|AvailabilityZoneSelection specifies how AZs should be selected if there are more AZs<br />in a region than specified by AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit. There are 2 selection schemes:<br />Ordered - selects based on alphabetical order<br />Random - selects AZs randomly in a region<br />Defaults to Ordered|"Ordered"|
|**availabilityZoneUsageLimit**|int|AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit specifies the maximum number of availability zones (AZ) that<br />should be used in a region when automatically creating subnets. |**emptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup**|bool|EmptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup specifies whether the default VPC security group ingress<br />and egress rules should be removed.<br /><br />By default, when creating a VPC, AWS creates a security group called `default` with ingress and egress<br />rules that allow traffic from anywhere. The group could be used as a potential surface attack and<br />it's generally suggested that the group rules are removed or modified appropriately.<br /><br />NOTE: This only applies when the VPC is managed by the Cluster API AWS controller.||
|**id**|str|ID is the vpc-id of the VPC this provider should use to create resources.||

|**privateDnsHostnameTypeOnLaunch**|"ip-name" | "resource-name"|PrivateDNSHostnameTypeOnLaunch is the type of hostname to assign to instances in the subnet at launch.<br />For IPv4-only and dual-stack (IPv4 and IPv6) subnets, an instance DNS name can be based on the instance IPv4 address (ip-name)<br />or the instance ID (resource-name). ### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedControlPlaneSpecOidcIdentityProviderConfig

IdentityProviderconfig is used to specify the oidc provider config to be attached with this eks cluster

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**clientId**|str|This is also known as audience. The ID for the client application that makes<br />authentication requests to the OpenID identity provider.||
|**groupsClaim**|str|The JWT claim that the provider uses to return your groups.||
|**groupsPrefix**|str|The prefix that is prepended to group claims to prevent clashes with existing<br />names (such as system: groups). For example, the valueoidc: will create group<br />names like oidc:engineering and oidc:infra.||
|**identityProviderConfigName**|str|The name of the OIDC provider configuration.<br /><br />IdentityProviderConfigName is a required field||
|**issuerUrl**|str|The URL of the OpenID identity provider that allows the API server to discover<br />public signing keys for verifying tokens. The URL must begin with https://<br />and should correspond to the iss claim in the provider's OIDC ID tokens.<br />Per the OIDC standard, path components are allowed but query parameters are<br />not. Typically the URL consists of only a hostname, like https://server.example.org<br />or https://example.com. This URL should point to the level below .well-known/openid-configuration<br />and must be publicly accessible over the internet.||
|**requiredClaims**|{str:str}|The key value pairs that describe required claims in the identity token.<br />If set, each claim is verified to be present in the token with a matching<br />value. |**tags**|{str:str}|tags to apply to oidc identity provider association||
|**usernameClaim**|str|The JSON Web Token (JWT) claim to use as the username. The default is sub,<br />which is expected to be a unique identifier of the end user. You can choose<br />other claims, such as email or name, depending on the OpenID identity provider.<br />Claims other than email are prefixed with the issuer URL to prevent naming<br />clashes with other plug-ins.||
|**usernamePrefix**|str|The prefix that is prepended to username claims to prevent clashes with existing<br />names. If you do not provide this field, and username is a value other than<br />email, the prefix defaults to issuerurl#. You can use the value - to disable<br />all prefixing.||

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedControlPlaneStatusFailureDomainsAnon

FailureDomainSpec is the Schema for Cluster API failure domains. It allows controllers to understand how many failure domains a cluster can optionally span across.

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2ROSAControlPlaneSpecDefaultMachinePoolSpec

DefaultMachinePoolSpec defines the configuration for the default machinepool(s) provisioned as part of the cluster creation. One MachinePool will be created with this configuration per AvailabilityZone. Those default machinepools are required for openshift cluster operators to work properly. As these machinepool not created using ROSAMachinePool CR, they will not be visible/managed by ROSA CAPI provider. `rosa list machinepools -c <rosaClusterName>` can be used to view those machinepools.  This field will be removed in the future once the current limitation is resolved.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**autoscaling**|[ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2ROSAControlPlaneSpecDefaultMachinePoolSpecAutoscaling](#controlplaneclusterxk8siov1beta2rosacontrolplanespecdefaultmachinepoolspecautoscaling)|autoscaling||
|**instanceType**|str|The instance type to use, for example `r5.xlarge`. Instance type ref; https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/instance-types/||
### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2ROSAControlPlaneSpecDefaultMachinePoolSpecAutoscaling

Autoscaling specifies auto scaling behaviour for the default MachinePool. Autoscaling min/max value must be equal or multiple of the availability zones count.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**maxReplicas**|int|max replicas||

### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2ROSAControlPlaneSpecExternalAuthProvidersItems0ClaimMappingsGroups

Groups is a name of the claim that should be used to construct groups for the cluster identity. The referenced claim must use array of strings values.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**claim** `required`|str|Claim is a JWT token claim to be used in the mapping||
|**prefix**|str|Prefix is a string to prefix the value from the token in the result of the<br />claim mapping.<br /><br />By default, no prefixing occurs.<br /><br />Example: if `prefix` is set to "myoidc:"" and the `claim` in JWT contains<br />an array of strings "a", "b" and  "c", the mapping will result in an<br />array of string "myoidc:a", "myoidc:b" and "myoidc:c".||
### ControlplaneClusterxK8sIoV1beta2ROSAControlPlaneSpecExternalAuthProvidersItems0ClaimMappingsUsername

Username is a name of the claim that should be used to construct usernames for the cluster identity.  Default value: "sub"

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**claim** `required`|str|Claim is a JWT token claim to be used in the mapping||
|**prefix**|str|Prefix is prepended to claim to prevent clashes with existing names.||
|**prefixPolicy**|"" | "NoPrefix" | "Prefix"|PrefixPolicy specifies how a prefix should apply.<br /><br />By default, claims other than `email` will be prefixed with the issuer URL to<br />prevent naming clashes with other plugins.<br /><br />Set to "NoPrefix" to disable prefixing.<br /><br />Example:<br />(1) `prefix` is set to "myoidc:" and `claim` is set to "username".<br />If the JWT claim `username` contains value `userA`, the resulting<br />mapped value will be "myoidc:userA".<br />(2) `prefix` is set to "myoidc:" and `claim` is set to "email". If the<br />JWT `email` claim contains value "userA@myoidc.tld", the resulting<br />mapped value will be "myoidc:userA@myoidc.tld".<br />(3) `prefix` is unset, `issuerURL` is set to `https://myoidc.tld`,<br />the JWT claims include "username":"userA" and "email":"userA@myoidc.tld",<br />and `claim` is set to:<br />(a) "username": the mapped value will be "https://myoidc.tld#userA"<br />(b) "email": the mapped value will be "userA@myoidc.tld"||

|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up machine images when<br />a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.<br />Supports substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base<br />OS and kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to look up machine images when a<br />machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.||

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**allowedCIDRBlocks**|[str]|AllowedCIDRBlocks is a list of CIDR blocks allowed to access the bastion host.<br />They are set as ingress rules for the Bastion host's Security Group (defaults to 0.0.0.0/0).||
|**ami**|str|AMI will use the specified AMI to boot the bastion. If not specified,<br />the AMI will default to one picked out in public space.||
|**disableIngressRules**|bool|DisableIngressRules will ensure there are no Ingress rules in the bastion host's security group.<br />Requires AllowedCIDRBlocks to be empty.||
|**enabled**|bool|Enabled allows this provider to create a bastion host instance<br />with a public ip to access the VPC private network.||
|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType will use the specified instance type for the bastion. If not specified,<br />Cluster API Provider AWS will use t3.micro for all regions except us-east-1, where t2.micro<br />will be the default.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneEndpoint

ControlPlaneEndpoint represents the endpoint used to communicate with the control plane.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**host** `required`|str|The hostname on which the API server is serving.||
|**port** `required`|int|The port on which the API server is serving.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancer

ControlPlaneLoadBalancer is optional configuration for customizing control plane behavior.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalListeners**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerAdditionalListenersItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspeccontrolplaneloadbalanceradditionallistenersitems0)]|AdditionalListeners sets the additional listeners for the control plane load balancer.<br />This is only applicable to Network Load Balancer (NLB) types for the time being.||
|**additionalSecurityGroups**|[str]|AdditionalSecurityGroups sets the security groups used by the load balancer. Expected to be security group IDs<br />This is optional - if not provided new security groups will be created for the load balancer||
|**crossZoneLoadBalancing**|bool|CrossZoneLoadBalancing enables the classic ELB cross availability zone balancing.<br /><br />With cross-zone load balancing, each load balancer node for your Classic Load Balancer<br />distributes requests evenly across the registered instances in all enabled Availability Zones.<br />If cross-zone load balancing is disabled, each load balancer node distributes requests evenly across<br />the registered instances in its Availability Zone only.<br /><br />Defaults to false.||
|**disableHostsRewrite**|bool|DisableHostsRewrite disabled the hair pinning issue solution that adds the NLB's address as 127.0.0.1 to the hosts<br />file of each instance. This is by default, false.||
|**healthCheck**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerHealthCheck](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspeccontrolplaneloadbalancerhealthcheck)|health check||
|**healthCheckProtocol**|"TCP" | "SSL" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS" | "TLS" | "UDP"|HealthCheckProtocol sets the protocol type for ELB health check target<br />default value is ELBProtocolSSL||
|**ingressRules**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerIngressRulesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspeccontrolplaneloadbalanceringressrulesitems0)]|IngressRules sets the ingress rules for the control plane load balancer.||
|**loadBalancerType**|"classic" | "elb" | "alb" | "nlb" | "disabled"|LoadBalancerType sets the type for a load balancer. The default type is classic.|"classic"|
|**name**|str|Name sets the name of the classic ELB load balancer. As per AWS, the name must be unique<br />within your set of load balancers for the region, must have a maximum of 32 characters, must<br />contain only alphanumeric characters or hyphens, and cannot begin or end with a hyphen. Once<br />set, the value cannot be changed.||
|**preserveClientIP**|bool|PreserveClientIP lets the user control if preservation of client ips must be retained or not.<br />If this is enabled 6443 will be opened to 0.0.0.0/0.||
|**scheme**|"internet-facing" | "internal"|Scheme sets the scheme of the load balancer (defaults to internet-facing)|"internet-facing"|
|**subnets**|[str]|Subnets sets the subnets that should be applied to the control plane load balancer (defaults to discovered subnets for managed VPCs or an empty set for unmanaged VPCs)||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerAdditionalListenersItems0HealthCheck

HealthCheck sets the optional custom health check configuration to the API target group.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**intervalSeconds**|int|The approximate amount of time, in seconds, between health checks of an individual<br />target.||
|**path**|str|The destination for health checks on the targets when using the protocol HTTP or HTTPS,<br />otherwise the path will be ignored.||
|**port**|str|The port the load balancer uses when performing health checks for additional target groups. When<br />not specified this value will be set for the same of listener port.||
|**protocol**|"TCP" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS"|||
|**thresholdCount**|int|The number of consecutive health check successes required before considering<br />a target healthy.||
|**timeoutSeconds**|int|The amount of time, in seconds, during which no response from a target means<br />a failed health check.||
|**unhealthyThresholdCount**|int|The number of consecutive health check failures required before considering<br />a target unhealthy.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerIngressRulesItems0

IngressRule defines an AWS ingress rule for security groups.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**cidrBlocks**|[str]|List of CIDR blocks to allow access from. Cannot be specified with SourceSecurityGroupID.||

|**fromPort** `required`|int|FromPort is the start of port range.||
|**ipv6CidrBlocks**|[str]|List of IPv6 CIDR blocks to allow access from. Cannot be specified with SourceSecurityGroupID.||
|**protocol** `required`|"-1" | "4" | "tcp" | "udp" | "icmp" | "58" | "50"|||
|**sourceSecurityGroupIds**|[str]|The security group id to allow access from. Cannot be specified with CidrBlocks.||
|**sourceSecurityGroupRoles**|[str]|The security group role to allow access from. Cannot be specified with CidrBlocks.<br />The field will be combined with source security group IDs if specified.||
|**toPort** `required`|int|ToPort is the end of port range.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkSubnetsItems0

SubnetSpec configures an AWS Subnet.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZone**|str|AvailabilityZone defines the availability zone to use for this subnet in the cluster's region.||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.||
|**id** `required`|str|ID defines a unique identifier to reference this resource.<br />If you're bringing your subnet, set the AWS subnet-id here, it must start with `subnet-`.<br /><br />When the VPC is managed by CAPA, and you'd like the provider to create a subnet for you,<br />the id can be set to any placeholder value that does not start with `subnet-`;<br />upon creation, the subnet AWS identifier will be populated in the `ResourceID` field and<br />the `id` field is going to be used as the subnet name. If you specify a tag<br />called `Name`, it takes precedence.||
|**ipv6CidrBlock**|str|IPv6CidrBlock is the IPv6 CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />A subnet can have an IPv4 and an IPv6 address.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isIpv6**|bool|IsIPv6 defines the subnet as an IPv6 subnet. A subnet is IPv6 when it is associated with a VPC that has IPv6 enabled.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isPublic**|bool|IsPublic defines the subnet as a public subnet. A subnet is public when it is associated with a route table that has a route to an internet gateway.||
|**natGatewayId**|str|NatGatewayID is the NAT gateway id associated with the subnet.<br />Ignored unless the subnet is managed by the provider, in which case this is set on the public subnet where the NAT gateway resides. It is then used to determine routes for private subnets in the same AZ as the public subnet.||
|**parentZoneName**|str|ParentZoneName is the zone name where the current subnet's zone is tied when<br />the zone is a Local Zone.<br /><br />The subnets in Local Zone or Wavelength Zone locations consume the ParentZoneName<br />to select the correct private route table to egress traffic to the internet.||
|**resourceID**|str|ResourceID is the subnet identifier from AWS, READ ONLY.<br />This field is populated when the provider manages the subnet.||
|**routeTableId**|str|RouteTableID is the routing table id associated with the subnet.||
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
|**zoneType**|"availability-zone" | "local-zone" | "wavelength-zone"|ZoneType defines the type of the zone where the subnet is created.<br /><br />The valid values are availability-zone, local-zone, and wavelength-zone.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type availability-zone (regular) is always selected to create cluster<br />resources, like Load Balancers, NAT Gateways, Contol Plane nodes, etc.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type local-zone or wavelength-zone is not eligible to automatically create<br />regular cluster resources.<br /><br />The public subnet in availability-zone or local-zone is associated with regular public<br />route table with default route entry to a Internet Gateway.<br /><br />The public subnet in wavelength-zone is associated with a carrier public<br />route table with default route entry to a Carrier Gateway.<br /><br />The private subnet in the availability-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry to a NAT Gateway created in that zone.<br /><br />The private subnet in the local-zone or wavelength-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry re-using the NAT Gateway in the Region (preferred from the<br />parent zone, the zone type availability-zone in the region, or first table available).||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpc

VPC configuration.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZoneSelection**|"Ordered" | "Random"|AvailabilityZoneSelection specifies how AZs should be selected if there are more AZs<br />in a region than specified by AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit. There are 2 selection schemes:<br />Ordered - selects based on alphabetical order<br />Random - selects AZs randomly in a region<br />Defaults to Ordered|"Ordered"|
|**availabilityZoneUsageLimit**|int|AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit specifies the maximum number of availability zones (AZ) that<br />should be used in a region when automatically creating subnets. If a region has more<br />than this number of AZs then this number of AZs will be picked randomly when creating<br />default subnets. Defaults to 3|3|
|**carrierGatewayId**|str|CarrierGatewayID is the id of the internet gateway associated with the VPC,<br />for carrier network (Wavelength Zones).||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />Defaults to 10.0.0.0/16.<br />Mutually exclusive with IPAMPool.||
|**emptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup**|bool|EmptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup specifies whether the default VPC security group ingress<br />and egress rules should be removed.<br /><br />By default, when creating a VPC, AWS creates a security group called `default` with ingress and egress<br />rules that allow traffic from anywhere. The group could be used as a potential surface attack and<br />it's generally suggested that the group rules are removed or modified appropriately.<br /><br />NOTE: This only applies when the VPC is managed by the Cluster API AWS controller.||
|**id**|str|ID is the vpc-id of the VPC this provider should use to create resources.||
|**internetGatewayId**|str|InternetGatewayID is the id of the internet gateway associated with the VPC.||
|**ipamPool**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcIpamPool](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecnetworkvpcipampool)|ipam pool||
|**ipv6**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcIPV6](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecnetworkvpcipv6)|ipv6||
|**privateDnsHostnameTypeOnLaunch**|"ip-name" | "resource-name"|PrivateDNSHostnameTypeOnLaunch is the type of hostname to assign to instances in the subnet at launch.<br />For IPv4-only and dual-stack (IPv4 and IPv6) subnets, an instance DNS name can be based on the instance IPv4 address (ip-name)<br />or the instance ID (resource-name). For IPv6 only subnets, an instance DNS name must be based on the instance ID (resource-name).||
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||

|**sourceSecurityGroupIds**|[str]|The security group id to allow access from. Cannot be specified with CidrBlocks.||
|**sourceSecurityGroupRoles**|[str]|The security group role to allow access from. Cannot be specified with CidrBlocks.<br />The field will be combined with source security group IDs if specified.||
|**toPort** `required`|int|ToPort is the end of port range.||

|**httpTokens**|"optional" | "required"|The state of token usage for your instance metadata requests.<br /><br />If the state is optional, you can choose to retrieve instance metadata with<br />or without a session token on your request. If you retrieve the IAM role<br />credentials without a token, the version 1.0 role credentials are returned.<br />If you retrieve the IAM role credentials using a valid session token, the<br />version 2.0 role credentials are returned.<br /><br />If the state is required, you must send a session token with any instance<br />metadata retrieval requests. |**instanceMetadataTags**|"enabled" | "disabled"|Set to enabled to allow access to instance tags from the instance metadata.<br />Set to disabled to turn off access to instance tags from the instance metadata.<br />For more information, see Work with instance tags using the instance metadata<br />(https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/Using_Tags.html#work-with-tags-in-IMDS).<br /><br />Default: disabled|"disabled"|

|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up machine images when<br />a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.<br />Supports substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base<br />OS and kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to look up machine images when a<br />machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.||
|**network**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetwork](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecnetwork)|network||
|**partition**|str|Partition is the AWS security partition being used. Defaults to "aws"||
|**region**|str|The AWS Region the cluster lives in.||
|**s3Bucket**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecS3Bucket](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecs3bucket)|s3 bucket||

|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the bastion host. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecBastion

|**ami**|str|AMI will use the specified AMI to boot the bastion. If not specified,<br />the AMI will default to one picked out in public space.||
|**disableIngressRules**|bool|DisableIngressRules will ensure there are no Ingress rules in the bastion host's security group.<br />Requires AllowedCIDRBlocks to be empty.||
|**enabled**|bool|Enabled allows this provider to create a bastion host instance<br />with a public ip to access the VPC private network.||
|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType will use the specified instance type for the bastion. If not specified,<br />Cluster API Provider AWS will use t3.micro for all regions except us-east-1, where t2.micro<br />will be the default.||
